CosmoBolognaLib
Free Software C++/Python libraries for cosmological calculations
analyzeChains.ipynb

This notebook is aimed to help in post-processing Markov chain Monte Carlo outputs

To see the notebook, click here: notebook

"cells": [
{
"cell_type": "markdown",
"metadata": {},
"source": [
"# Introduction\n",
"\n",
"This notebook is aimed to help in post-processing Markov chain Monte Carlo outputs.\n",
"\n",
"It implements basic steps of the MCMC chain analysis, that can be followd to understand\n",
"if the posterior sampling has gone well. In particular, this notebook is used to:\n",
"\n",
"- understand chain convergence \n",
"- compute statistical quantities of the chain\n",
"- plot basic results\n",
"\n",
"We suggest to run the MCMC chains with burn_in=0 and thin=1, to \n",
"have full control of the output. \n",
"\n",
"The notebook will read the output of the CosmoBolognaLib posterior sampling.\n",
"\n",
"For a similar example, have a look at the emcee page: http://dfm.io/emcee/current/user/line/"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "code",
"execution_count": 1,
"metadata": {},
"outputs": [],
"source": [
"import os\n",
"import numpy as np\n",
"import matplotlib.pyplot as plt\n",
"import matplotlib.gridspec as gridspec\n",
"%matplotlib inline"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "markdown",
"metadata": {},
"source": [
"# Run the CosmoBolognaLib ./fit example"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "code",
"execution_count": 2,
"metadata": {},
"outputs": [
{
"data": {
"text/plain": [
"0"
]
},
"execution_count": 2,
"metadata": {},
"output_type": "execute_result"
}
],
"source": [
"#This is (of course) not mandatory. Here is done to have some example chain to plot.\n",
"os.system(\"make && ./fit\")"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "markdown",
"metadata": {},
"source": [
"# Read the MCMC output\n",
"\n",
"The basic inputs nedeed are the following:\n",
"\n",
"- the chain file\n",
"- the directory where it is stored"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "code",
"execution_count": 3,
"metadata": {},
"outputs": [],
"source": [
"inputDir = \"../output/\"\n",
"inputFilePar = \"chains_linear_relation_parameters.dat\"\n",
"inputFile = \"chains_linear_relation_chain.dat\""
]
},
{
"cell_type": "markdown",
"metadata": {},
"source": [
"Read all the columns of the table:\n",
"\n",
"- the first column is the step number, the last three columns are the values of the log likelihood, the log prior and the log posterior\n",
"\n",
"- all the other columns are the parameters, whose names are inferred from the header file \n",
"\n",
"- fixed parameters are identified as the ones with null standard deviation; there is currently no way \n",
" (and maybe there is no need) to recognize derived parameters"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "code",
"execution_count": 4,
"metadata": {},
"outputs": [],
"source": [
"table = np.genfromtxt(inputDir+inputFile, unpack=True)\n",
"\n",
"nPar = len(table)-4"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "code",
"execution_count": 5,
"metadata": {},
"outputs": [],
"source": [
"ff = open(inputDir+inputFilePar, \"r\")\n",
"\n",
"ff.readline()\n",
"\n",
"isFree = [True]*nPar\n",
"nParEff = 0\n",
"names = [\"\"]*(nPar+4)\n",
"names[0] = \"Step\"\n",
"names[-1] = \"Log(Posterior)\"\n",
"names[-2] = \"Log(Prior)\"\n",
"names[-3] = \"Log(Likelihood)\"\n",
"for i in range(nPar):\n",
" ll = ff.readline()\n",
" if \"FREE\" in ll:\n",
" names[i+1] = ll[0:ll.index(\"FREE\")]\n",
" nParEff += 1\n",
" if \"FIXED\" in ll:\n",
" names[i+1] = ll[0:ll.index(\"FIXED\")]\n",
" isFree[i] = False"
]
},
{
"cell_type": "markdown",
"metadata": {},
"source": [
"## Plot the chains\n",
"\n",
"By plotting the chains you should be able to roughly identified the step\n",
"at which chains are converged. This should be used below as burn in."
]
},
